GT Equivalence Verification (CRK11)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)**

Key observations about the GT:
- It has an A² term
- It has a sin(√A) term
- It does NOT depend on t
- The sin(√A) function is a specific transcendental function that cannot be represented by exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, or power functions

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. For a candidate to match, it must:
1. Be able to eliminate any t-dependence (by setting relevant constants to 0)
2. Contain basis functions that can reproduce sin(√A)

**sin(√A)** is a very specific function. It CANNOT be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials in A
- exp(c*A) or exp(c*√A)
- log functions
- Rational functions of A
- Power functions A^c
- A/(A+c) type terms
- Max(0,A)^c terms
- |A|^c terms
- Combinations of the above

This is because sin(√A) is an oscillatory function (for large A) while all the above are monotonic or have different analytic properties. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, none of these can exactly equal sin(√A).

Let me check each candidate for the presence of sin(√A) or equivalent:

Going through all 50 candidates, I see that **none of them contain a sin() function or any trigonometric function**. They all use combinations of:
- Polynomials (A², A, constants)
- Exponentials (exp)
- Logarithms (log)
- Rational functions (A/(A+c))
- Power functions (A^c)
- Absolute values (|A|^c)
- Max functions

Since sin(√A) is linearly independent from all these basis functions, and the coefficient of sin(√A) in the GT is 0.5985 ≠ 0, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify this conclusion by confirming the GT truly requires the sin term: The GT is -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A). The sin(√A) term has a non-zero coefficient, so it cannot be ignored.
